style="color: #000000;">SMITH &amp; WESSON</font></h2> <h2><font style="color: #000000;"><span>Model 642 Centennial Airweight .38 Special +P 1.875 Inch Barrel Matte Stainless Finish Double Action Black Grips 5 Round</span></font></h2> <h2><span><font style="color: #000000;"><span>Double action only. J-Small frame. Five round capacity. Internal hammer. .312 smooth target trigger. Serrated ramp front sight. Fixed notch rear sight. Black rubber grips. Aluminum alloy frame, stainless steel cylinder. Matte silver finish.</span></font><br></span></h2> <p><span>&nbsp;</span>The ultimate backup and concealed carry handgun has arrived, bringing revolvers into the twenty first century.</p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <p>The Smith &amp; Wesson J-Frame has become the most popular small frame personal defense revolver on the market. With decades of reliable performance to its credit, the J-frame line offers models capable of firing .22 LR, .22 Magnum, .38 S&amp;W Special and the more powerful .357 Magnum loads. &nbsp;Smith &amp; Wesson offers these revolvers from our production, M&amp;P, Pro Series, and Classics lines in three diverse hammer designs; internal, exposed and shrouded.&nbsp;</p> <p><img We bought it new but after only 2 weeks the trigger started stacking on about the 3rd shot and if it was rapid fired the cylinder would hang up a little. The trigger pull was awful. The dealer sent it back to S&amp;W and 5 weeks later it is a fine operating tool.</div> <div class="Row"> By <span class="Text"> Mr. Q</span> from <span class="Text"> Wisconsin</span></div> </div> </div> </td> </tr><tr> <td class="ReviewItem"> <div class="ItemStyle"> <div class="Title"> <span class="Subject"> One oof the Best Carry Guns</span>, November 05, 2015</div> <div class="Content"> <div class="StarRating"> <img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"></div> <div class="Row"> I've owned a number of S&amp;W firearms over the years and they have always been excellent. This J-frame is no exception. For years, it has been THE carry pistol of choice, and even today, with all the compact and sub-compact semiauto options available, a great many knowledgeable shooters still carry this one. I own two. One for my wife, outfitted with Pachmayr Grippers to help absorb recoil and give her more grip surface, and one foe me, which I outfitted with finger-groove rosewood combat grips. The grips have made a huge difference in my ability not only to carry it concealed, but to shoot it more accurately. In my experience, while rubber grips do help to absorb recoil, they tend not to carry as well, and also have a tendency to move slightly in your grip while shooting, which can affect accuracy. The grips I have are similar to what S&amp;W provides on their Ladysmith revolvers (in fact, the same company makes them)and I don't believe they can be improved on. I've had many full-sized pistols and revolvers over the years, all of which have eventually been sold or traded. (And some of those I wish I still had! You know how that goes.)This one is a keeper.</div> <div class="Row"> By <span class="Text"> Simon</span> from <span class="Text"> North Carolina</span></div> </div> </div> </td> </tr><tr> <td class="ReviewItem"> <div class="ItemStyle"> <div class="Title"> <span class="Subject"> 642</span>, November 18, 2014</div> <div class="Content"> <div class="StarRating"> <img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/ShadeStar.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/ShadeStar.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/ShadeStar.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"></div> <div class="Row"> Disappointment is hardly a word I would use with a Smith Wesson product but it is the first thought that comes to mind with my 642. Finish is good fit is not. Required a trigger job to be acceptable and after firing 500 rounds the cylinder closes and locks much better. For the guy hunitng rattlesnakes in the review (lehigh acres - Florida), there is a mechanism lock on the side that locks the mechanism. If it is locked, it will not cock or shoot with a trigger pull, that's what a lock is for. Unlock the gun and it will fire much better.</div> <div class="Row"> By <span class="Text"> D</span> from <span class="Text"> Missouri</span></div> </div> </div> </td> </tr><tr> <td class="ReviewItem"> <div class="ItemStyle"> <div class="Title"> <span class="Subject"> Very fine hand gun</span>, November 10, 2012</div> <div class="Content"> <div class="StarRating"> <img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"><img src="/themes/New5/Images/Star.gif" valign="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"></div> <div class="Row"> I am very happy with this revolver.
